An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n65: // selector.\\n66: //\\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n101: //\\n102: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\\n127: //\\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\\n131: // to something else, for example through a\\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\\n133: //\\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\\n138: \\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\\n139: \\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\\n140: \\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\\n141: \\t// different handlers.\\n142: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\\n143: \\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\\n144: \\t// seen every item in the initial list).\\n145: \\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n146: \\t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\\n147: \\t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\\n148: \\t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\\n149: \\t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\\n150: \\t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\\n151: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-150\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5891151c-1aea-4dc0-908c-79cbbcf64012","uuid":"7f58c0d5-a79e-4596-8446-a05fe3219dd1","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: package cache\\n18: \\n19: import (\\n20: \\t\\\"errors\\\"\\n21: \\t\\\"fmt\\\"\\n22: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"time\\\"\\n24: \\n25: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\\\"\\n26: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\\\"\\n27: \\tutilruntime \\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\\\"\\n28: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\\\"\\n29: \\t\\\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\\\"\\n30: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\\\"\\n31: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/clock\\\"\\n32: \\n33: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n34: \\n35: \\tclientgofeaturegate \\\"k8s.io/client-go/features\\\"\\n36: )\\n37: \\n38: // SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\\n39: // clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\\n40: // objects. To be formally complete, we say that the\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n65: // selector.\n66: //\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\n73: //\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n75: // during `Run()`.\n76: //\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\n84: //\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n91: //\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n96: // into its constituent parts.\n97: //\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n101: //\n102: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n127: //\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n131: // to something else, for example through a\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n133: //\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\n138: \t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n139: \t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n140: \t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n141: \t// different handlers.\n142: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n143: \t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n144: \t// seen every item in the initial list).\n145: \tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n146: \t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\n147: \t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\n148: \t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\n149: \t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\n150: \t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-150"}}}

Architecture in client-go v0.32.0\\n\\nThe SharedInformer factory is the core mechanism in Kubernetes client-go for maintaining an eventually-consistent local cache of API server resources. The implementation spans multiple key components:\\n\\n### Factory Registration (informers/factory.go)\\nThe `SharedInformerFactory` interface and `sharedInformerFactory` implementation in `informers/factory.go` provides the main entry point. Functions like `NewSharedInformerFactory()` and `NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions()` create factory instances. The factory manages:\\n- A map of informers indexed by object type\\n- Tracking of started vs unstarted informers\\n- Resync period configuration (global and per-type)\\n- Namespace filtering and list option tweaking\\n- Shutdown coordination via WaitGroup\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- `Start()` initializes all registered informers in separate goroutines\\n- `Shutdown()` stops all informers and waits for cleanup\\n- `WaitForCacheSync()` waits for cache synchronization to complete\\n- `InformerFor()` gets or creates a SharedIndexInformer for a given object\\n\\n### Informer Registration (informers/internalinterfaces/factory_interfaces.go)\\nThe internal `SharedInformerFactory` interface defines the minimal contract needed to avoid import cycles. The `NewInformerFunc` type is a function pointer that creates SharedIndexInformers, allowing the factory to instantiate informers for different resource types.\\n\\n### List-Watch Mechanism (tools/cache/listwatch.go)\\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface combines:\\n- `List()` method to fetch all objects matching criteria\\n- `Watch()` method to receive incremental updates\\n\\nThe `ListWatch` implementation provides a concrete instance that wraps REST client calls. `NewListWatchFromClient()` creates ListWatch instances for specific resources, handling field selector configuration and options modification.\\n\\n### Reflector Pattern (tools/cache/reflector.go)\\nThe `Reflector` watches a resource via ListerWatcher and syncs all changes to a Store. Key features:\\n- Handles List/Watch semantics with exponential backoff for failures\\n- Manages resource version tracking for resumable watches\\n- Supports pagination with `WatchListPageSize` for large datasets\\n- Implements optional watchlist streaming mode (UseWatchList)\\n- Customizable error handling via WatchErrorHandler\\n- Resync period support for reconciliation\\n\\nThe Reflector is created by the Controller and drives continuous synchronization with the API server.\\n\\n### Cache Store Implementations (tools/cache/store.go, tools/cache/index.go)\\nThe `Store` interface defines basic cache operations (Add, Update, Delete, Get, List, Replace). The `Indexer` extends Store with indexing capabilities for efficient lookups by field values.\\n\\n`NewStore()` creates a basic unindexed store using `ThreadSafeStore` as the backend.\\n`NewIndexer()` creates an indexed store with configurable index functions.\\n\\n### Thread-Safe Storage (tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go)\\nThe `ThreadSafeStore` interface provides concurrent-safe access to cached objects. Implementation uses:\\n- Mutex-protected access to object maps\\n- Index structures for efficient field-based queries (NamespaceIndex, etc.)\\n- Support for adding indexers dynamically\\n\\n### DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)\\nThe `DeltaFIFO` is a producer-consumer queue that:\\n- Stores objects as Deltas (sequence of operations: Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync)\\n- Acts as the intermediary between Reflector (producer) and event handlers (consumers)\\n- Tracks known objects to detect state changes\\n- Supports deduplication and ordering guarantees\\n\\n`NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions()` creates instances with configurable key function and known object tracking.\\n\\n### Controller Orchestration (tools/cache/controller.go)\\nThe `Controller` interface orchestrates the Reflector and DeltaFIFO queue:\\n- Created via `New()` with a Config specifying the queue, ListerWatcher, and ProcessFunc\\n- `Run()` method starts the Reflector in a goroutine and processes queue items\\n- Handles both initial sync and incremental updates\\n\\n### SharedInformer Event Distribution (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)\\nThe `SharedIndexInformer` implementation:\\n- Wraps a Controller and Indexer (the cache)\\n- Uses `sharedProcessor` to distribute cache events to multiple listeners\\n- Each listener is wrapped in a `processorListener` with its own event channel\\n- Supports AddEventHandler() to register ResourceEventHandlers\\n- Provides HasSynced() to check if initial sync is complete\\n- Uses synctrack.Lazy for lazy evaluation of sync state\\n\\n`NewSharedIndexInformer()` creates instances with optional indexers for performance.\\n\\n### Synchronization Tracking (tools/cache/synctrack/)\\nThe synctrack package provides utilities for tracking sync state across multiple goroutines:\\n- `AsyncTracker` helps propagate HasSynced in multi-threaded scenarios\\n- `Lazy` provides lazy evaluation with single computation\\n- `SingleFileTracker` tracks sync state for individual listeners\\n\\n### Complete Flow\\n1. User calls `NewSharedInformerFactory()` to create a factory\\n2. User calls `factory.Start(stopChan)` to initialize all registered informers\\n3. Factory creates informers via `InformerFor()` using NewInformerFuncs\\n4. Each informer creates a SharedIndexInformer with cache (Indexer) and controller\\n5. Controller creates a Reflector with ListerWatcher and DeltaFIFO queue\\n6. Reflector starts `ListAndWatch()` which:\\n   - Calls ListerWatcher.List() to fetch initial objects\\n   - Stores all objects in the DeltaFIFO with Replaced deltas\\n   - Calls ListerWatcher.Watch() to receive incremental updates\\n   - Adds updates to DeltaFIFO as Added/Updated/Deleted deltas\\n7. Controller.Run() processes items from DeltaFIFO:\\n   - Pops Deltas and applies them to the Indexer (cache)\\n   - Invokes registered event handlers\\n8. SharedProcessor distributes events to multiple listeners\\n9. Clients query cache via Indexer.Get() or Lister interfaces\\n10. User calls `factory.Shutdown()` to cleanly stop all informers\\n\\nThis architecture provides an eventually-consistent, efficient, and scalable mechanism for keeping local caches in sync with Kubernetes API server state.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2578,"cache_read_input_tokens":84338,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2578},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5891151c-1aea-4dc0-908c-79cbbcf64012","uuid":"aa3b25d9-b165-41f9-86b6-2ca7a8b3c3a9"}

Architecture in client-go v0.32.0\\n\\nThe SharedInformer factory is the core mechanism in Kubernetes client-go for maintaining an eventually-consistent local cache of API server resources. The implementation spans multiple key components:\\n\\n### Factory Registration (informers/factory.go)\\nThe `SharedInformerFactory` interface and `sharedInformerFactory` implementation in `informers/factory.go` provides the main entry point. Functions like `NewSharedInformerFactory()` and `NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions()` create factory instances. The factory manages:\\n- A map of informers indexed by object type\\n- Tracking of started vs unstarted informers\\n- Resync period configuration (global and per-type)\\n- Namespace filtering and list option tweaking\\n- Shutdown coordination via WaitGroup\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- `Start()` initializes all registered informers in separate goroutines\\n- `Shutdown()` stops all informers and waits for cleanup\\n- `WaitForCacheSync()` waits for cache synchronization to complete\\n- `InformerFor()` gets or creates a SharedIndexInformer for a given object\\n\\n### Informer Registration (informers/internalinterfaces/factory_interfaces.go)\\nThe internal `SharedInformerFactory` interface defines the minimal contract needed to avoid import cycles. The `NewInformerFunc` type is a function pointer that creates SharedIndexInformers, allowing the factory to instantiate informers for different resource types.\\n\\n### List-Watch Mechanism (tools/cache/listwatch.go)\\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface combines:\\n- `List()` method to fetch all objects matching criteria\\n- `Watch()` method to receive incremental updates\\n\\nThe `ListWatch` implementation provides a concrete instance that wraps REST client calls. `NewListWatchFromClient()` creates ListWatch instances for specific resources, handling field selector configuration and options modification.\\n\\n### Reflector Pattern (tools/cache/reflector.go)\\nThe `Reflector` watches a resource via ListerWatcher and syncs all changes to a Store. Key features:\\n- Handles List/Watch semantics with exponential backoff for failures\\n- Manages resource version tracking for resumable watches\\n- Supports pagination with `WatchListPageSize` for large datasets\\n- Implements optional watchlist streaming mode (UseWatchList)\\n- Customizable error handling via WatchErrorHandler\\n- Resync period support for reconciliation\\n\\nThe Reflector is created by the Controller and drives continuous synchronization with the API server.\\n\\n### Cache Store Implementations (tools/cache/store.go, tools/cache/index.go)\\nThe `Store` interface defines basic cache operations (Add, Update, Delete, Get, List, Replace). The `Indexer` extends Store with indexing capabilities for efficient lookups by field values.\\n\\n`NewStore()` creates a basic unindexed store using `ThreadSafeStore` as the backend.\\n`NewIndexer()` creates an indexed store with configurable index functions.\\n\\n### Thread-Safe Storage (tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go)\\nThe `ThreadSafeStore` interface provides concurrent-safe access to cached objects. Implementation uses:\\n- Mutex-protected access to object maps\\n- Index structures for efficient field-based queries (NamespaceIndex, etc.)\\n- Support for adding indexers dynamically\\n\\n### DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)\\nThe `DeltaFIFO` is a producer-consumer queue that:\\n- Stores objects as Deltas (sequence of operations: Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync)\\n- Acts as the intermediary between Reflector (producer) and event handlers (consumers)\\n- Tracks known objects to detect state changes\\n- Supports deduplication and ordering guarantees\\n\\n`NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions()` creates instances with configurable key function and known object tracking.\\n\\n### Controller Orchestration (tools/cache/controller.go)\\nThe `Controller` interface orchestrates the Reflector and DeltaFIFO queue:\\n- Created via `New()` with a Config specifying the queue, ListerWatcher, and ProcessFunc\\n- `Run()` method starts the Reflector in a goroutine and processes queue items\\n- Handles both initial sync and incremental updates\\n\\n### SharedInformer Event Distribution (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)\\nThe `SharedIndexInformer` implementation:\\n- Wraps a Controller and Indexer (the cache)\\n- Uses `sharedProcessor` to distribute cache events to multiple listeners\\n- Each listener is wrapped in a `processorListener` with its own event channel\\n- Supports AddEventHandler() to register ResourceEventHandlers\\n- Provides HasSynced() to check if initial sync is complete\\n- Uses synctrack.Lazy for lazy evaluation of sync state\\n\\n`NewSharedIndexInformer()` creates instances with optional indexers for performance.\\n\\n### Synchronization Tracking (tools/cache/synctrack/)\\nThe synctrack package provides utilities for tracking sync state across multiple goroutines:\\n- `AsyncTracker` helps propagate HasSynced in multi-threaded scenarios\\n- `Lazy` provides lazy evaluation with single computation\\n- `SingleFileTracker` tracks sync state for individual listeners\\n\\n### Complete Flow\\n1. User calls `NewSharedInformerFactory()` to create a factory\\n2. User calls `factory.Start(stopChan)` to initialize all registered informers\\n3. Factory creates informers via `InformerFor()` using NewInformerFuncs\\n4. Each informer creates a SharedIndexInformer with cache (Indexer) and controller\\n5. Controller creates a Reflector with ListerWatcher and DeltaFIFO queue\\n6. Reflector starts `ListAndWatch()` which:\\n   - Calls ListerWatcher.List() to fetch initial objects\\n   - Stores all objects in the DeltaFIFO with Replaced deltas\\n   - Calls ListerWatcher.Watch() to receive incremental updates\\n   - Adds updates to DeltaFIFO as Added/Updated/Deleted deltas\\n7. Controller.Run() processes items from DeltaFIFO:\\n   - Pops Deltas and applies them to the Indexer (cache)\\n   - Invokes registered event handlers\\n8. SharedProcessor distributes events to multiple listeners\\n9. Clients query cache via Indexer.Get() or Lister interfaces\\n10. User calls `factory.Shutdown()` to cleanly stop all informers\\n\\nThis architecture provides an eventually-consistent, efficient, and scalable mechanism for keeping local caches in sync with Kubernetes API server state.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
